   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">São Tomé and Príncipe</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in the Gulf of Guinea
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the islands of the sovereign state, see <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_Island" title="São Tomé Island">São Tomé Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Príncipe">Príncipe</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="São Tomé (disambiguation)">São Tomé (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Principe_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Principe (disambiguation)">Principe (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>São Tomé and Príncipe</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">aʊ</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span></span> ...<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> <span style="font-size:85%;">Portuguese:&nbsp;</span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[sɐ̃w̃ tuˈmɛ i ˈpɾĩsɨpɨ]</a></span>), (English: <b>Saint Thomas and Prince</b>) officially the <b>Democratic Republic of São Tomé and Príncipe</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">República Democrática de São Tomé e Príncipe</i>), is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a>, off the western equatorial coast of <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It consists of two <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagos</a> around the two main islands of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_Island" title="São Tomé Island">São Tomé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Príncipe">Príncipe</a>, about 140&nbsp;km (87&nbsp;mi) apart and about 250 and 225&nbsp;km (155 and 140&nbsp;mi) off the northwestern coast of <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>. </p>
      <p>The islands were uninhabited until their discovery by <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> explorers in the 15th century. Gradually colonized and settled by the Portuguese throughout the 16th century, they collectively served as a vital commercial and trade center for the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>. The rich volcanic soil and proximity to the Equator made São Tomé and Príncipe ideal for <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> cultivation, followed later by cash crops such as <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a>; the lucrative plantation economy was heavily dependent upon imported African slaves. Cycles of social unrest and economic instability throughout the 19th and 20th centuries culminated in peaceful <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> in 1975. São Tomé and Príncipe has since remained one of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>'s most stable and <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a> countries. </p>
      <p>With a population of 201,800 (2018 official estimate),<sup id="cite_ref-auto_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-5">[5]</a></sup> São Tomé and Príncipe is the second-smallest African <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> after <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>, as well as the smallest <a href="/wiki/List_of_territorial_entities_where_Portuguese_is_an_official_language" class="mw-redirect" title="List of territorial entities where Portuguese is an official language">Portuguese-speaking country</a>. Its people are predominantly of African and <i><a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o#Mestiço_–_São_Tomé_and_Príncipe" title="Mestiço">mestiço</a></i> descent, with most practicing <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Catholic Christianity</a>. The legacy of Portuguese rule is also visible in the country's culture, customs, and music, which fuse European and African influences. São Tomé and Príncipe is a founding member state of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="History of São Tomé and Príncipe">History of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">

        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geological_history">Geological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The two islands that make up what is called São Tomé and Príncipe were formed 30 million years ago during the <a href="/wiki/Oligocene" title="Oligocene">Oligocene</a> era, due to volcanic activity beneath deep water along the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Cameroon Line">Cameroon Line</a>. The volcanic soils of <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phonolite" title="Phonolite">phonolites</a>, dating to 3 million years, have been used for plantation crops since colonial times. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_of_Europeans">Arrival of Europeans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Arrival of Europeans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The islands of São Tomé and Príncipe were uninhabited when the Portuguese arrived sometime around 1470. The first Europeans to put ashore were <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_de_Santar%C3%A9m" title="João de Santarém">João de Santarém</a> and <a href="/wiki/P%C3%AAro_Escobar" title="Pêro Escobar">Pêro Escobar</a>. Portuguese navigators explored the islands and decided that they would be good locations for bases to trade with the mainland. </p>
      <p>The dates of European arrival are sometimes given as 21 December (<a href="/wiki/Thomas_the_Apostle" title="Thomas the Apostle">St Thomas's Day</a>) 1471, for São Tomé; and 17 January (<a href="/wiki/Anthony_the_Great" title="Anthony the Great">St Antony's Day</a>) 1472, for Príncipe, though other sources cite different years around that time. Príncipe was initially named <i>Santo Antão</i> ("Saint Anthony"), changing its name in 1502 to <i>Ilha do Príncipe</i> ("Prince's Island"), in reference to the Prince of Portugal to whom duties on the island's sugar crop were paid. </p>
      <p>The first successful settlement of São Tomé was established in 1493 by <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Caminha" title="Álvaro Caminha">Álvaro Caminha</a>, who received the land as a grant from the crown.<sup id="cite_ref-Bijela_pčela_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bijela_pčela-12">[12]</a></sup> Príncipe was settled in 1500 under a similar arrangement. Attracting settlers proved difficult, however, and most of the earliest inhabitants were "undesirables" sent from Portugal, mostly <a href="/wiki/Spanish_and_Portuguese_Jews" title="Spanish and Portuguese Jews">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In time, these settlers found the volcanic soil of the region suitable for agriculture, especially the growing of sugar. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Portuguese_S.C3.A3o_Tom.C3.A9_and_Pr.C3.ADncipe"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_São_Tomé_and_Príncipe">Portuguese São Tomé and Príncipe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Portuguese São Tomé and Príncipe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Portuguese São Tomé and Príncipe">Portuguese São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>By 1515, São Tomé and Príncipe had become slave depots for the coastal slave trade centered at <a href="/wiki/Elmina" title="Elmina">Elmina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bakewell_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakewell-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> The cultivation of sugar was a labour-intensive process and the Portuguese began to enslave large numbers of Africans from the mainland. These slaves originated mainly from the Gold Coast, Niger Delta and in Kongo.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In the sugar boom's early stages, property on the islands had little value, with farming for local consumption while the economy relied mainly on the transit of slaves, though already many foodstuffs were imported.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">[16]</a></sup> When the local landowner Álvaro Borges died in 1504, his cleared land and domesticated animals were sold for only 13,000 réis, about the price of three slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Valentim_Fernandes" title="Valentim Fernandes">Valentim Fernandes</a> around 1506, São Tomé had more sugarcane fields than <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> "from which they already produce molasses,"<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> but the island lacked facilities for industrial sugar production.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_(8084256064).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%288084256064%29.jpg/220px-Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%288084256064%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%288084256064%29.jpg/330px-Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%288084256064%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%288084256064%29.jpg/440px-Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%288084256064%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="1936"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Forte_de_S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_-_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_(8084256064).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Sebasti%C3%A3o_Museum" title="São Sebastião Museum">São Sebastião Museum</a> in São Tomé
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_development_in_the_16th_century">Economic development in the 16th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Economic development in the 16th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>São Tomé would only become economically noteworthy with the introduction of a water-powered sugar mill in 1515, which soon led to the mass cultivation of sugar:<sup id="cite_ref-:1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-19">[19]</a></sup> "The fields are expanding and the sugar mills, too. At this time, only two sugar mills are here and another three are being built, counting the mill of the contractors, which is large. Similarly, the necessary conditions exist, such as streams and timber, to be able to build many more. And the [sugar] canes are the biggest I have ever seen in my life." Sugar <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantations</a> were organized with slave labor, and by the mid-16th century, the Portuguese settlers had turned the islands into Africa's foremost exporter of sugar.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Slaves in São Tomé were bought from the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Coast_of_West_Africa" title="Slave Coast of West Africa">Slave Coast of West Africa</a>, the Niger Delta, the island of Fernando Po, and later from the Kongo and Angola.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> In the 16th century, the enslaved were imported from and exported to Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Elmina" title="Elmina">Elmina</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a>, Angola, and the Spanish Americas. In 1510, reportedly 10,000 to 12,000 slaves were imported by Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1516, São Tomé received 4,072 slaves with the purpose of re-exportation.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-22">[22]</a></sup> From 1519 to 1540, the island was the center of the slave trade between Elmina and the Niger Delta.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Throughout the early to mid sixteenth century, São Tomé traded in slaves intermittently with Angola and the Kingdom of Kongo.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In 1525 São Tomé began trafficking slaves to the Spanish Americas, mainly to the Caribbean and Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> From 1532 to 1536, São Tomé sent an annual average of 342 slaves to the <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-26">[26]</a></sup> Prior to 1580, the island accounted for 75 percent of Brazil's imports, mainly slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-26">[26]</a></sup> The slave trade remained a cornerstone of São Tomé's economy until after 1600. </p>
      <p>The power dynamics of São Tomé in the 16th century were surprisingly diverse with the participation of free <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">mulatto</a>[s] and black citizens in governance. Voluntary colonists shunned São Tomé for its disease and food shortages, so the Portuguese crown deported convicts to the island and encouraged interracial relationships to secure the colony. Slavery was also not permanent, as demonstrated through the 1515 royal decree granting the manumission of African wives of white settlers and their mixed-race children.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1517, another decree freed the male slaves who had originally arrived on the island with the first colonists.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-27">[27]</a></sup> After 1520, a royal charter allowed for property-owning, married, free mulattos to hold public offices.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-27">[27]</a></sup> This was followed by a decree in 1546 establishing civil equality between these qualified mulattos and the white settlers,<sup id="cite_ref-:4_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-27">[27]</a></sup> allowing free mulattos and black citizens opportunities for upward mobility and participation in local politics and business. Social divisions led to frequent disputes within the colony's town councils and with the governor and bishop,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> with constant political unstability. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg/220px-Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg/330px-Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg/440px-Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="605"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Insula_S._Thomae-1645.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Capture of São Tomé by <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_Jol" title="Cornelis Jol">Cornelis Jol</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> in 1641.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At first, slavery in São Tomé was less strict. In the mid-16th century, an anonymous Portuguese pilot noted that the slaves were employed as couples, built their own accommodations, and worked autonomously once a week on the cultivation of their own food supply.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> However, this more relaxed slave system did not last long following the introduction of plantations. Throughout, slaves frequently ran away to the inhospitable mountain forests of the island's interior.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">[30]</a></sup> Between 1514 and 1527, five percent of slaves that were imported to São Tomé escaped, often to starve,<sup id="cite_ref-:5_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> though 1531-1535 saw major food shortages even in the plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> Eventually, the <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (people)">Maroon people</a> developed settlements in the interior known as<i> macambos</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slave_rebellions">Slave rebellions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Slave rebellions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The first signs of slave rebellion began in the 1530s, when the maroon gangs organized to attack plantations, some of which were abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> A formal complaint was lodged by local Portuguese authorities in 1531 lamenting that too many settlers and black citizens were being killed in the attacks, and that the island would be lost if the problem remained unresolved.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> In a 1533 'bush war', a 'bush captain' led militia units to suppress the maroons.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> A significant event in the maroon fight for freedom occurred in 1549, when two men claiming to be free-born were taken in from the <i>macambos </i>by a wealthy mulatto planter named Ana de Chaves.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> With the support of de Chaves, the two men petitioned the king to be declared free, and the request was approved. The largest population of marroons coincided with the sugar boom of the mid-16th century, as the plantations teemed with slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_31-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-31">[31]</a></sup> Between 1587 and 1590, many of the runaway slaves were defeated in another bush war.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-32">[32]</a></sup> By 1593, the governor declared the maroon forces almost completely extinguished.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Nevertheless, maroon populations kept settlers away from the southern and western regions. </p>
      <p>The greatest slave revolt occurred in July 1595, when the government was weakened by disputes between the bishop and the governor. A native slave named Amador recruited 5000 slaves to raid and destroy plantations, sugar mills, and settler houses.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-32">[32]</a></sup> Amador's rebellion made three raids on the town and destroyed 60 of the island's 85 sugar mills, but were defeated by the militia after three weeks. Two hundred slaves were killed in combat, and Amador and the other rebel leaders were executed, while the rest of the slaves were granted amnesty and returned to their plantations. So ended one of the greatest slave uprisings to that time.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-32">[32]</a></sup> Smaller slave rebellions followed in the 17th and 18th centuries. </p> 
      <h4><span id="S.C3.A3o_Tom.C3.A9_and_Pr.C3.ADncipe_in_the_18th.2C_19th_and_20th_centuries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="São_Tomé_and_Príncipe_in_the_18th,_19th_and_20th_centuries">São Tomé and Príncipe in the 18th, 19th and 20th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: São Tomé and Príncipe in the 18th, 19th and 20th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Eventually, competition from sugar-producing colonies in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a> began to hurt the islands. The large enslaved population also proved difficult to control, with Portugal unable to invest many resources in the effort. Sugar cultivation thus declined over the next 100 years, and by the mid-17th century, São Tomé had become primarily a transit point for ships engaged in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">slave trade</a> between continental Africa and the Americas. </p>
      <p>In the early 19th century, two new cash crops, coffee and cocoa, were introduced. The rich volcanic soils proved well suited to the new crops, and soon extensive plantations (known as <i>roças</i>), owned by Portuguese companies or absentee landlords, occupied almost all of the good farmland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By 1908, São Tomé had become the world's largest producer of cocoa, which remains the country's most important crop. </p>
      <p>The <i>roças</i> system, which gave the plantation managers a high degree of authority, led to abuses against the African farm workers. Although Portugal officially abolished slavery in 1876, the practice of forced paid labour continued. <i><a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a></i> documented in words and pictures the continued use of slaves in São Tomé in its 13 March 1897 issue. </p>
      <p>In the early 20th century, an internationally publicized controversy arose over charges that <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angolan</a> contract workers were being subjected to forced labour and unsatisfactory working conditions. Sporadic labor unrest and dissatisfaction continued well into the 20th century, culminating in an outbreak of riots in 1953 in which several hundred African laborers were killed in a clash with their Portuguese rulers. The anniversary of this "<a href="/wiki/Batep%C3%A1_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Batepá Massacre">Batepá Massacre</a>" remains officially observed by the government. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Independence_.281975.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1975)">Independence (1975)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Independence (1975)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_(16223085806).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_%2816223085806%29.jpg/220px-Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_%2816223085806%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_%2816223085806%29.jpg/330px-Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_%2816223085806%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_%2816223085806%29.jpg/440px-Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_%2816223085806%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sao_Tome_Cathedral_7_(16223085806).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The cathedral of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9" title="São Tomé">São Tomé</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>By the late 1950s, when other emerging nations across the African continent demanded their independence, a small group of São Toméans had formed the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Movement for the Liberation of São Tomé and Príncipe">Movement for the Liberation of São Tomé and Príncipe</a> (MLSTP), which eventually established its base in nearby <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>. Picking up momentum in the 1960s, events moved quickly after the overthrow of the <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Caetano" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcelo Caetano">Caetano</a> dictatorship in Portugal in April 1974. </p>
      <p>The new Portuguese regime was committed to the dissolution of its overseas colonies. In November 1974, their representatives met with the MLSTP in Algiers and worked out an agreement for the transfer of sovereignty. After a period of transitional government, São Tomé and Príncipe achieved independence on 12 July 1975, choosing as the first president the MLSTP Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Pinto_da_Costa" title="Manuel Pinto da Costa">Manuel Pinto da Costa</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1990, São Tomé became one of the first African countries to undergo <a href="/wiki/Democratization" title="Democratization">democratic reform</a>, and changes to the constitution – the legalization of opposition political parties – led to elections in 1991 that were nonviolent, free, and transparent. <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Trovoada" title="Miguel Trovoada">Miguel Trovoada</a>, a former prime minister who had been in exile since 1986, returned as an independent candidate and was elected president. Trovoada was re-elected in São Tomé's second multiparty presidential election in 1996. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Convergence_Party_%E2%80%93_Reflection_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Convergence Party – Reflection Group">Party of Democratic Convergence</a> won a majority of seats in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of São Tomé and Príncipe">National Assembly</a>, with the MLSTP becoming an important and vocal minority party. Municipal elections followed in late 1992, in which the MLSTP won a majority of seats on five of seven regional councils. In early legislative elections in October 1994, the MLSTP won a plurality of seats in the assembly. It regained an outright majority of seats in the November 1998 elections. </p>
      <p>Presidential elections were held in July 2001. The candidate backed by the <a href="/wiki/Independent_Democratic_Action" title="Independent Democratic Action">Independent Democratic Action</a> party, <a href="/wiki/Fradique_de_Menezes" title="Fradique de Menezes">Fradique de Menezes</a>, was elected in the first round and inaugurated on 3 September. Parliamentary elections were held in March 2002. For the next four years, a series of short-lived opposition-led governments was formed. </p>
      <p>The army seized power for one week in July 2003, complaining of corruption and that forthcoming oil revenues would not be divided fairly. An accord was negotiated under which President de Menezes was returned to office.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cohabitation_(government)" title="Cohabitation (government)">cohabitation</a> period ended in March 2006, when a propresidential coalition won enough seats in National Assembly elections to form a new government.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 30 July 2006 presidential election, Fradique de Menezes easily won a second five-year term in office, defeating two other candidates <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Trovoada" title="Patrice Trovoada">Patrice Trovoada</a> (son of former President Miguel Trovoada) and independent <a href="/wiki/Nilo_Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Nilo Guimarães">Nilo Guimarães</a>. Local elections, the first since 1992, took place on 27 August 2006 and were dominated by members of the ruling coalition.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 12 February 2009, a<i> <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> </i>was attempted to overthrow President Fradique de Menezes. The plotters were imprisoned, but later received a pardon from President de Menezes.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Evaristo_Carvalho" title="Evaristo Carvalho">Evaristo Carvalho</a> has been the President of São Tomé and Príncipe since <a href="/wiki/2016_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9an_presidential_election" title="2016 São Toméan presidential election">2016 elections</a>, after winning the incumbent President <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Pinto_da_Costa" title="Manuel Pinto da Costa">Manuel Pinto da Costa</a>. President Carvalho is also Vice president of the Independent Democratic Action party (ADI). <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Emery_Trovoada" class="mw-redirect" title="Patrice Emery Trovoada">Patrice Emery Trovoada</a> was Prime Minister since 2014 and he is the leader of Independent Democratic Action party (ADI).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In December 2018, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Bom_Jesus" title="Jorge Bom Jesus">Jorge Bom Jesus</a>, the leader of the Movimento de Libertação de São Tomé e Príncipe-Partido Social Democráta (MLSTP-PSD), was sworn in as new prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Politics of São Tomé and Príncipe">Politics of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_(7).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%287%29.jpg/220px-Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%287%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%287%29.jpg/330px-Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%287%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%287%29.jpg/440px-Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%287%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Palais_pr%C3%A9sidentiel_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_(7).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_e_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Presidential Palace of São Tomé e Príncipe">Presidential Palace of São Tomé e Príncipe</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The president of the republic is elected to a five-year term by direct <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Secret_ballot" title="Secret ballot">secret ballot</a>, and must gain an outright majority to be elected. The president may hold up to two consecutive terms. The prime minister is appointed by the president, and the 14 members of cabinet are chosen by the prime minister. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of São Tomé and Príncipe">National Assembly</a>, the supreme organ of the state and the highest legislative body, is made up of 55 members, who are elected for a four-year term and meet semiannually. Justice is administered at the highest level by the Supreme Court. The judiciary is independent under the current constitution. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe has functioned under a multiparty system since 1990. With regard to <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Human rights in São Tomé and Príncipe">human rights</a>, there are guarantees on freedom of speech and the freedom to form opposition political parties. </p>
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe finished 11th out of the African countries measured by the <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a> in 2010, a comprehensive reflection of the levels of governance in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>São Tomé and Principe is considered a <a href="/wiki/Free_Country_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Country (politics)">free country</a>, with very high freedom of speech, high political freedom and average <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a>. In terms of <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>, São Tomé and Principe is a country with average corruption, although in recent years this level has been decreasing.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In tourism terms, the risk is low, equivalent to the risk of visiting <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Foreign relations of São Tomé and Príncipe">Foreign relations of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe has embassies in Angola, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, Gabon, Portugal, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. It <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe_relations" title="China–São Tomé and Príncipe relations">recognized</a> the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> in 2016. It also has a permanent mission to the UN in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and an International Diplomatic Correspondent Office. </p>
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe is a founding member state of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, also known as the Lusophone Commonwealth, and international organization and political association of <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations across four continents, where <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is an official language. </p>
      <p>The countries with the best relations with São Tomé and Príncipe are <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> has historical ties with São Tomé and Príncipe, from the period of colonization by the Portuguese. Portugal is the largest investor in São Tomé and Príncipe, investing millions of euros in the economy of São Tomé and Príncipe. São Tomé and Príncipe maintains an embassy in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, a consulate in <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a> and one in <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a>. Portugal maintains an embassy in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9" title="São Tomé">São Tomé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:11_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-41">[41]</a></sup> Portugal and São Tomé and Príncipe signed an agreement, in which Portugal undertakes to patrol the coastal area of São Tomé and Príncipe, protecting it mainly from pirates. The Portuguese military ship <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Navy" title="Portuguese Navy">NRP Zaire</a> and some Portuguese patrol boats are permanently stationed on the coast of São Tomé and Príncipe.<sup id="cite_ref-Portugal_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portugal-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:11_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-41">[41]</a></sup> The economy of São Tomé and Príncipe is closely linked to that of Portugal, with Portugal accounting for more than 50% of imports from São Tomé and Príncipe. Portugal has also helped to develop education in São Tomé and Príncipe, financially helping to build and maintain the Public University of São Tomé and Príncipe.<sup id="cite_ref-aulp.org_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aulp.org-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Portugal_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portugal-42">[42]</a></sup> The Portuguese President <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Rebelo_de_Sousa" title="Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa">Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa</a> visited Sao Tome and Principe in 2018 to demonstrate the strong economic and cultural ties between <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and São Tome and Principe.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Angola">Angola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Angola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> is a major business partner mainly in the area of natural energy resources, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> is the major supplier of <a href="/wiki/Oil_spill" title="Oil spill">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> to São Tomé and Príncipe. In addition, hundreds of Angolan tourists visit São Tomé and Príncipe every year, contributing to the local economy. There is a relatively large community of Angolans in São Tomé and Príncipe. São Tomé and Príncipe maintains an embassy in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> and Angola maintains an embassy in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9" title="São Tomé">São Tomé</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_Now_-_Official_Site_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_Now_-_Official_Site-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_080123-N-4044H-052_Chief_Hospital_Corpsman_Chris_Maurer_demonstrates_to_Sao_Tomain_military_personnel_the_procedure_for_inserting_an_intravenous_drip_into_a_person%27s_vein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/US_Navy_080123-N-4044H-052_Chief_Hospital_Corpsman_Chris_Maurer_demonstrates_to_Sao_Tomain_military_personnel_the_procedure_for_inserting_an_intravenous_drip_into_a_person%27s_vein.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/US_Navy_080123-N-4044H-052_Chief_Hospital_Corpsman_Chris_Maurer_demonstrates_to_Sao_Tomain_military_personnel_the_procedure_for_inserting_an_intravenous_drip_into_a_person%27s_vein.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/US_Navy_080123-N-4044H-052_Chief_Hospital_Corpsman_Chris_Maurer_demonstrates_to_Sao_Tomain_military_personnel_the_procedure_for_inserting_an_intravenous_drip_into_a_person%27s_vein.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2520" data-file-height="1800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_080123-N-4044H-052_Chief_Hospital_Corpsman_Chris_Maurer_demonstrates_to_Sao_Tomain_military_personnel_the_procedure_for_inserting_an_intravenous_drip_into_a_person%27s_vein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Santomean personnel undergo medical training with US Naval corpsmen
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> has had relations with São Tomé and Príncipe since 1975, and has offered millions of dollars in financial aid packages to São Tomé and Príncipe. The financial aid packages were designed to develop the country's infrastructure and improve its fiscal, tax and customs administration. In addition, in recent years, some <a href="/wiki/US_Coast_guard" class="mw-redirect" title="US Coast guard">US Coast Guard</a> ships have visited São Tomé and Príncipe, providing medical and military training to soldiers from São Tomé and Príncipe. In 2002, the US had plans to establish a small <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_military_bases" title="List of United States military bases">military base</a> on the island of São Tomé, São Tomé and Príncipe accepted the construction of the base, but the plan was canceled due to US political and financial issues. In 1992, the US federal government broadcaster, <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a>, and the government of São Tomé signed a long-term agreement to establish a relay broadcasting station in São Tomé. Voice of America currently broadcasts to much of Africa from this facility.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Wikipedia_and_sources_that_mirror_or_use_it" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="This claim cites another Wikipedia article. Articles need references to reliable third-party sources. (April 2021)">circular reference</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Others">Others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Thousands of tourists from <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> visit São Tomé and Príncipe, helping the local economy. Relations between Cape Verde and São Tomé and Príncipe have improved over the years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> have been increasing commercial ties with São Tomé and Príncipe, buying more and more cocoa and other products from São Tomé and Príncipe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> also has very good relations with São Tomé and Príncipe, investing thousands of euros annually in the agricultural sector.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> has contributed to improving the health and education system in São Tomé and Príncipe, Brazilian television channels and films are the most watched in São Tomé and Príncipe.<sup id="cite_ref-aulp.org_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aulp.org-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Neighboring <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Congo">Republic of Congo</a> are important partners in São Tomé and Príncipe, many companies in these countries have establishments and businesses in São Tomé and Príncipe. Because these countries speak <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, the language has become important in the business sector (together with <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>), in São Tomé and Príncipe.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_Now_-_Official_Site_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography_Now_-_Official_Site-45">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2013, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> has invested in some road and sea port projects but investments have been stalling in recent years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of São Tomé and Príncipe">Military of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe's military is small and consists of four branches: the Army (<i>Exército</i>), Coast Guard (<i>Guarda Costeira</i> also called "Navy"), Presidential Guard (<i>Guarda Presidencial</i>), and the National Guard.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, São Tomé and Príncipe signed the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Districts of São Tomé and Príncipe">Districts of São Tomé and Príncipe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Autonomous Region of Príncipe">Autonomous Region of Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1977, two years after independence, the country was divided into two provinces (São Tomé Province and Príncipe Province) and six districts. Since the new constitution was adopted in 1990, the provinces have been abolished, and the districts are the only administrative subdivisions. Since 29 April 1995, the island of Príncipe is an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Autonomous Region of Príncipe">autonomous region</a>, coterminous with the district of Pagué. The larger island of São Tomé is divided into six <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Districts of São Tomé and Príncipe">districts</a> and Príncipe island into one:<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><b>São Tomé Island</b> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/%C3%81gua_Grande_District" title="Água Grande District">Água Grande</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Cantagalo_District" title="Cantagalo District">Cantagalo</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Cau%C3%A9_District" title="Caué District">Caué</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Lemb%C3%A1_District" title="Lembá District">Lembá</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Lobata_District" title="Lobata District">Lobata</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9-Z%C3%B3chi_District" title="Mé-Zóchi District">Mé-Zóchi</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p><b>Príncipe Island</b> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_of_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Autonomous Region of Príncipe">Pagué</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Geography of São Tomé and Príncipe">Geography of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:552px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg/550px-Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg" decoding="async" width="550" height="79" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg/825px-Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg/1100px-Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="300"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Sao_Tome_WV_banner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>A view of <i><a href="/wiki/Praia_Inhame" title="Praia Inhame">Praia Inhame</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Cau%C3%A9_District" title="Caué District">Caué District</a>, São Tomé.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The islands of São Tomé and Príncipe, situated in the equatorial Atlantic and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">Gulf of Guinea</a> about 300 and 250&nbsp;km (190 and 160&nbsp;mi), respectively, off the northwest coast of <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, constitute Africa's second-smallest country. Both are part of the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_line" title="Cameroon line">Cameroon volcanic mountain line</a>, which also includes the islands of <a href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n" title="Annobón">Annobón</a> to the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">Bioko</a> to the northeast (both part of <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon" title="Mount Cameroon">Mount Cameroon</a> on the coast of Gulf of Guinea. </p>
      <p>São Tomé is 50&nbsp;km (30&nbsp;mi) long and 30&nbsp;km (20&nbsp;mi) wide and the more mountainous of the two islands. Its peaks reach 2,024&nbsp;m (6,640&nbsp;ft) – <a href="/wiki/Pico_de_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9" title="Pico de São Tomé">Pico de São Tomé</a>. Príncipe is about 30&nbsp;km (20&nbsp;mi) long and 6&nbsp;km (4&nbsp;mi) wide. Its peaks reach 948&nbsp;m (3,110&nbsp;ft) – <a href="/wiki/Pico_de_Pr%C3%ADncipe" class="mw-redirect" title="Pico de Príncipe">Pico de Príncipe</a>. Swift streams radiating down the mountains through lush forest and cropland to the sea cross both islands. The Equator lies immediately south of São Tomé Island, passing through the islet <a href="/wiki/Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas" title="Ilhéu das Rolas">Ilhéu das Rolas</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Pico_C%C3%A3o_Grande" title="Pico Cão Grande">Pico Cão Grande</a> (Great Dog Peak) is a landmark <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_plug" title="Volcanic plug">volcanic plug</a> peak, at 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994658806"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;params=0_7_0_N_6_34_00_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">0°7′0″N</span> <span class="longitude">6°34′00″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">0.11667°N 6.56667°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">0.11667; 6.56667</span></span></span></a></span> in southern São Tomé. It rises over 300&nbsp;m (1,000&nbsp;ft) above the surrounding terrain and the summit is 663&nbsp;m (2,175&nbsp;ft) above sea level. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%283%29.jpg/300px-S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%283%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%283%29.jpg/450px-S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%283%29.jpg/600px-S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_-_Ilh%C3%A9u_das_Rolas_-_Praia_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ilhéu das Rolas
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>At sea level, the climate is tropical—hot and humid with average yearly temperatures of about 27&nbsp;°C (80.6&nbsp;°F) and little daily variation. The temperature rarely rises beyond 32&nbsp;°C (89.6&nbsp;°F). At the interior's higher elevations, the average yearly temperature is 20&nbsp;°C (68&nbsp;°F), and nights are generally cool. Annual rainfall varies from 5,000&nbsp;mm (196.9&nbsp;in) on the southwestern slopes to 1,000&nbsp;mm (39.4&nbsp;in) in the northern lowlands. The rainy season is from October to May. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Wildlife of São Tomé and Príncipe">Wildlife of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's territory is part of the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9,_Pr%C3%ADncipe,_and_Annob%C3%B3n_moist_lowland_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="São Tomé, Príncipe, and Annobón moist lowland forests">São Tomé, Príncipe, and Annobón moist lowland forests</a> ecoregion.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-50">[50]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.64/10, ranking it 68th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe does not have a large number of native mammals (although the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_shrew" title="São Tomé shrew">São Tomé shrew</a> and several bat species are <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a>). The islands are home to a larger number of endemic birds and plants, including the world's smallest ibis (the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_ibis" title="São Tomé ibis">São Tomé ibis</a>), the world's largest sunbird (the <a href="/wiki/Giant_sunbird" title="Giant sunbird">giant sunbird</a>), the rare <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_fiscal" title="São Tomé fiscal">São Tomé fiscal</a>, and several giant species of <i><a href="/wiki/Begonia" title="Begonia">Begonia</a></i>. São Tomé and Principe is an important marine turtle-nesting site, including the <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawksbill turtle">hawksbill turtles</a> (<i>Eretmochelys imbricata</i>). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Economy of São Tomé and Príncipe">Economy of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Since the 19th century, the economy of São Tomé and Príncipe has been based on plantation agriculture. At the time of independence, Portuguese-owned plantations occupied 90% of the cultivated area. After independence, control of these plantations passed to various state-owned agricultural enterprises. The main crop on São Tomé is cocoa, representing about 95% of agricultural exports. Other export crops include copra, palm kernels, and coffee. </p>
      <p>Domestic food-crop production is inadequate to meet local consumption, so the country imports most of its food.<sup id="cite_ref-AMD_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMD-52">[52]</a></sup> As of 1997, an estimated 90% of the country's food needs were met through imports.<sup id="cite_ref-AMD_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMD-52">[52]</a></sup> Efforts have been made by the government in recent years to expand food production, and several projects have been undertaken, largely financed by foreign donors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Other than agriculture, the main economic activities are fishing and a small industrial sector engaged in processing local agricultural products and producing a few basic consumer goods. The scenic islands have potential for tourism, and the government is attempting to improve its rudimentary tourist industry infrastructure. The government sector accounts for about 11% of employment. </p>
      <p>Following independence, the country had a centrally directed economy, with most means of production owned and controlled by the state. The original constitution guaranteed a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>, with privately owned cooperatives combined with publicly owned property and means of production. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_measures">Government measures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Government measures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the 1980s and 1990s, the economy of São Tomé encountered major difficulties. Economic growth stagnated, and cocoa exports dropped in both value and volume, creating large balance-of-payments deficits. Plantation land was seized, resulting in the complete collapse of cocoa production. At the same time, the international price of cocoa slumped. </p>
      <p>In response to its economic downturn, the government undertook a series of far-reaching economic reforms. In 1987, the government implemented an <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> <a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">structural adjustment</a> program, and invited greater private participation in management of the <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprise" title="State-owned enterprise">parastatals</a>, as well as in the agricultural, commercial, banking, and tourism sectors. The focus of economic reform since the early 1990s has been widespread privatization, especially of the state-run agricultural and industrial sectors. </p>
      <p>The São Toméan government has traditionally obtained foreign assistance from various donors, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UN Development Programme</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the European Union, Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>. In April 2000, in association with the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Central Bank of São Tomé and Príncipe">Banco Central de São Tomé e Príncipe</a>, the IMF approved a poverty-reduction and growth facility for São Tomé aimed at reducing inflation to 3% for 2001, raising ideal growth to 4%, and reducing the fiscal deficit. </p>
      <p>In late 2000, São Tomé qualified for significant debt reduction under the IMF–World Bank's <a href="/wiki/Heavily_Indebted_Poor_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Heavily Indebted Poor Countries">Heavily Indebted Poor Countries</a> initiative. The reduction is being reevaluated by the IMF, due to the attempted <i>coup d'état</i> in July 2003 and subsequent emergency spending. Following the truce, the IMF decided to send a mission to São Tomé to evaluate the macroeconomic state of the country. This evaluation is ongoing, reportedly pending oil legislation to determine how the government will manage incoming oil revenues, which are still poorly defined, but in any case expected to change the economic situation dramatically. </p>
      <p>In parallel, some efforts have been made to incentivize private tourism initiatives, but their scope remains limited.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>São Tomé also hosts a broadcasting station of the American <a href="/wiki/International_Broadcasting_Bureau" title="International Broadcasting Bureau">International Broadcasting Bureau</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a><sup id="cite_ref-WRTH1995p162_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRTH1995p162-54">[54]</a></sup> at Pinheira.<sup id="cite_ref-WRTH1997p514_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WRTH1997p514-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Portugal remains one of São Tomé's major trading partners, particularly as a source of imports. Food, manufactured articles, machinery, and transportation equipment are imported primarily from the EU. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_challenges">Economic challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economic challenges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In the past few years, the economy of São Tomé and Príncipe has grown, driven by <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, tourism and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_investments" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign investments">foreign investments</a>, but mainly grew due to government spending driven by foreign loans. Gross domestic product (GDP) grew at an average rate of 5.5% between 2009 and 2017, but has slowed since 2014. The slowdown in economic growth was caused by lower government spending due to decreased foreign loans and decreased revenue government tax.<sup id="cite_ref-Overview_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overview-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The biggest challenges for the economy of São Tomé and Príncipe are limited workforce, the fact that São Tomé and Príncipe is an archipelago, small domestic market, climatic fluctuations, global warming, scarce diplomatic resources and reducing poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-Overview_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overview-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For long-term economic growth, the government is trying to stimulate various sectors of the economy, diversify the economy, cut government spending and encourage private sector and foreign investment.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Positive_aspects">Positive aspects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Positive aspects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe outperforms the sub-Saharan Africa average on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> and has made great progress on most social indicators. All children in São Tomé and Príncipe are enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/Education_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Education system">education system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> has increased to 70 years, the <a href="/wiki/Infant_Mortality_Rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant Mortality Rate">infant mortality rate</a> has decreased dramatically and the vast majority of the population already has access to piped water and access to electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In terms of business, the government of São Tomé and Príncipe has passed several laws that facilitate the creation of private businesses and foreign investments. Between 2015 and 2019 the number of businesses and small businesses increased a lot. This increase led to a decrease in unemployment, an increase in exports and the creation of several manufactures. In the coming years a significant economic increase is expected.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The tourism sector has great potential to be a way of diversifying the country's economy. This sector has been expanding with the increase of foreign investment. Large resorts have been built on the beaches of São Tomé and Príncipe.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-58">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transports">Transports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The main <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">ports</a> in the country are in the city of São Tomé and Neves, both on the island of São Tomé, which were very degraded were modernized in 2014. Close to the city of São Tomé, the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_International_Airport" title="São Tomé International Airport">international airport</a> was expanded and modernized. The telephone system and the road network are good by African standards. The use of the cell phone is widely used and has been improved in recent years. The <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet service</a> is available and has been widely installed in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:8_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Petroleum_exploration">Petroleum exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Petroleum exploration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2001, São Tomé and Nigeria reached agreement on joint exploration for petroleum in waters claimed by the two countries of the <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta_province" class="mw-redirect" title="Niger Delta province">Niger Delta geologic province</a>. After a lengthy series of negotiations, in April 2003, the joint development zone (JDZ) was opened for bids by international oil firms. The JDZ was divided into nine blocks; the winning bids for block one, <a href="/wiki/ChevronTexaco" class="mw-redirect" title="ChevronTexaco">ChevronTexaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>, and the Norwegian firm, Equity Energy, were announced in April 2004, with São Tomé to take in 40% of the $123&nbsp;million bid, and Nigeria the other 60%. Bids on other blocks were still under consideration in October 2004. São Tomé has received more than $2 million from the bank to develop its petroleum sector.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking">Banking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Banking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Central Bank of São Tomé and Príncipe">Banco Central de Sāo Tomé e Príncipe</a> is the central bank, responsible for monetary policy and bank supervision.
