Six banks are in the country; the largest and oldest is <a href="/wiki/Banco_Internacional_de_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_e_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Banco Internacional de São Tomé e Príncipe">Banco Internacional de São Tomé e Príncipe</a>, which is a subsidiary of Portugal's government-owned <a href="/wiki/Caixa_Geral_de_Dep%C3%B3sitos" title="Caixa Geral de Depósitos">Caixa Geral de Depósitos</a>. It had a monopoly on commercial banking until a change in the banking law in 2003 led to the entry of several other banks. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_partners">Business partners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Business partners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Exports">Exports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Exports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In 2018, exports from São Tomé and Príncipe totaled 24 million euros, an increase of 118% in 5 years, as in 2013 exports from São Tomé and Príncipe totaled only 11 million euros. Half of São Tomé and Príncipe's exports are <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa beans</a>. One fifth of exports are electrical machines. Other considerable exports are parts of airplanes, cars, iron, plastics, agricultural products (pepper, oils, nuts and beef).<sup id="cite_ref-:9_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-61">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The main destinations for exports from São Tomé and Príncipe are <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">Europe</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> (19%), <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> (14%), <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> (13%), <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (7%) and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (6%) stand out. Others important buyers are <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:251px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_(2018).png" class="image"><img alt="The most important import partners of Sao Tome and Principe (2018)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_%282018%29.png/249px-The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_%282018%29.png" decoding="async" width="249" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_%282018%29.png/374px-The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_%282018%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_%282018%29.png/498px-The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_%282018%29.png 2x" data-file-width="809" data-file-height="761"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_most_important_import_partners_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe_(2018).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The most important import partners of Sao Tome and Principe (2018)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the last 10 years, the countries in which the value of exports increased the most were <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. There was a sharp decrease in exports from São Tomé and Príncipe to <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Imports">Imports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Imports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In 2018, imports from São Tomé and Príncipe totaled 161 million euros. Since 2013, imports have been decreasing, albeit at a slow pace, since in 2013 imports totaled 167 million euros. A fifth of imports from São Tomé and Príncipe corresponded to <a href="/wiki/Refined_oil_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Refined oil products">refined oil</a> (mainly from Angola). Other important imports, in order of importance, were cars, rice, cereals, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>, electronic equipment, chemicals, clothing, meat, medical equipment, and wood.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 51%, more than half of the imports from São Tomé and Príncipe come from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>. A fifth of imports come from <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>, about 6% come from China, 4% from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">USA</a>, 4% from <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, 2% from <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> and 2% from <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the last 10 years, the countries in which the value of imports increased the most were <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. There was a sharp decrease in imports from <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_60-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-60">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal_2">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>From Portugal, what São Tomé and Príncipe imports most are machines, mainly electric generators, and computers, a lot of food, mainly wine, wheat, rice, milk, and soy oil. In addition, São Tomé and Príncipe also import in considerable quantities from Portugal, cars, soap, and iron. Portugal mainly buys scrap material, copper, cocoa, and clothing.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Demographics of São Tomé and Príncipe">Demographics of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dimanche_en_famille_sur_la_plage_des_Tamarins_(S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9)_(4).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dimanche_en_famille_sur_la_plage_des_Tamarins_%28S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9%29_%284%29.jpg/220px-Dimanche_en_famille_sur_la_plage_des_Tamarins_%28S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9%29_%284%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dimanche_en_famille_sur_la_plage_des_Tamarins_%28S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9%29_%284%29.jpg/330px-Dimanche_en_famille_sur_la_plage_des_Tamarins_%28S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9%29_%284%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Dimanche_en_famille_sur_la_plage_des_Tamarins_%28S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9%29_%284%29.jpg/440px-Dimanche_en_famille_sur_la_plage_des_Tamarins_%28S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9%29_%284%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a>

         </div>Santomeans on the beach, Lobata District
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_(56).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%2856%29.jpg/220px-Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%2856%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%2856%29.jpg/330px-Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%2856%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%2856%29.jpg/440px-Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_%2856%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tchiloli_%C3%A0_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_(56).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A scene of Santomean <i>Tchioli</i>, Auto de Floripes Festival
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The total population is estimated at 201,800 in May 2018 by the government agency.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-11">[11]</a></sup> About 193,380 people live on São Tomé and 8,420 on Príncipe. Natural increase is about 4,000 people per year. </p>
      <p>Nearly all are descended from people from different countries taken to the islands by the Portuguese from 1470 onwards. In the 1970s, two significant population movements occurred — the exodus of most of the 4,000 Portuguese residents and the influx of several hundred São Tomé refugees from Angola. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Distinct ethnic groups on São Tomé and Príncipe include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i>Mestiços</i>, or mixed-blood, are descendants of Portuguese colonists and African slaves brought to the islands during the early years of settlement from <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> (these people also are known as <i>filhos da terra</i> or "children of the land").</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angolares&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Angolares (page does not exist)">Angolares</a></i> are reputedly descendants of Angolan slaves who survived a 1540 shipwreck and now earn their livelihood fishing.</li> 
       <li><i>Forros</i> are descendants of freed slaves when slavery was abolished.</li> 
       <li><i>Serviçais</i> are contract laborers from Angola, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, living temporarily on the islands.</li> 
       <li><i>Tongas</i> are children of<i> serviçais</i> born on the islands.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europeans</a>, primarily Portuguese</li> 
       <li>Asians, mostly <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Macanese_people" title="Macanese people">Macanese people</a> of mixed Portuguese and Chinese descent from <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:maroon; width:2.4%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.4%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Languages of São Tomé and Príncipe">Languages of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is the official and the <i>de facto</i> national language of São Tomé and Príncipe, with about 98.4% speaking it, a significant share as their native language, and it has been spoken in the islands since the end of the 15th century. Restructured variants of Portuguese or <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese creole">Portuguese creoles</a> are also spoken: <a href="/wiki/Forro_Creole" title="Forro Creole">Forro</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole language</a> (36.2%), <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">Cape Verdean Creole</a> (8.5%), <a href="/wiki/Angolar_Creole" title="Angolar Creole">Angolar</a> (6.6%), and <a href="/wiki/Principense_Creole" title="Principense Creole">Principense</a> (1%). <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> (6.8%) and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> (4.9%) are foreign languages taught in schools. </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black"> 
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:LimeGreen"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 47.826161647115px; border-left-color:Yellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Yellow"></div>
         <div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:98.109051744333px 19.354946805086px 0 0; border-top-color:Orange"></div> 
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Orange"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in São Tomé and Príncipe <sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Forum_-_Religion_in_São_Tomé_and_Principe_(2010)_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Forum_-_Religion_in_São_Tomé_and_Principe_(2010)-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Orange; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> (71.9%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Yellow; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> (10.2%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:LimeGreen; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other or Non Religious (17.9%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of residents belongs to the local branch of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, which in turn retains close ties with the church in Portugal. Sizeable <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> minorities of <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventists</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Protestants">Evangelical Protestants</a> exist, as well as a small but growing <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> population. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

      </div>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>See <a href="/wiki/Health_in_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Health in São Tomé and Príncipe">Health in São Tomé and Príncipe</a> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Education in São Tomé and Príncipe is compulsory for four years.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-64">[64]</a></sup> Primary school enrollment and attendance rates were unavailable for São Tomé and Príncipe as of 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The educational system has a shortage of classrooms, insufficiently trained and underpaid teachers, inadequate textbooks and materials, high rates of repetition, poor educational planning and management, and a lack of community involvement in school management.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-64">[64]</a></sup> Domestic financing of the school system is lacking, leaving the system highly dependent on foreign financing.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-64">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tertiary institutions are the <a href="/wiki/National_Lyceum" title="National Lyceum">National Lyceum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="University of São Tomé and Príncipe">University of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>São Toméan <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a> is a mixture of <a href="/wiki/African_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="African culture">African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese culture">Portuguese</a> influences. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Music of São Tomé and Príncipe">Music of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <p>São Toméans are known for <i>ússua</i> and <i>socopé</i> <a href="/wiki/Rhythm" title="Rhythm">rhythms</a>, while Príncipe is home to the <i>dêxa</i> beat. Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Ballroom" title="Ballroom">ballroom</a> may have played an integral part in the development of these rhythms and their associated dances. </p>
      <p><i>Tchiloli</i> is a musical dance performance that tells a dramatic story. The danço-Congo is similarly a combination of music, dance, and theatre. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Literature of São Tomé and Príncipe">Literature of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_writers_by_country#São_Tomé_and_Príncipe" title="List of African writers by country">List of writers from São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div>
      <p>São Tomé and Príncipe's Portuguese-language literature and poetry is considered some of the richest in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_African_countries" title="Portuguese-speaking African countries">Lusophone Africa</a>. Other literature from the country has been written in <a href="/wiki/Forro_Creole" title="Forro Creole">Forro Creole</a>, English and Caué Creole. <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jos%C3%A9_Tenreiro" title="Francisco José Tenreiro">Francisco José Tenreiro</a> is considered one of the country's most influential writers. Other notable literary figures include <a href="/wiki/Manuela_Margarido" title="Manuela Margarido">Manuela Margarido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alda_Espirito_Santo" class="mw-redirect" title="Alda Espirito Santo">Alda Espirito Santo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olinda_Beja" title="Olinda Beja">Olinda Beja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Lima" title="Conceição Lima">Conceição Lima</a>. </p>
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Cuisine of São Tomé and Príncipe">Cuisine of São Tomé and Príncipe</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Staple_foods" class="mw-redirect" title="Staple foods">Staple foods</a> include <a href="/wiki/Fish_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fish (food)">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, and cooked <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Becker_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Becker-66">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tropical_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical fruit">Tropical fruits</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">pineapple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avocado" title="Avocado">avocado</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, are significant components of the cuisine. The use of hot spices is prominent in São Tomése cuisine.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-65">[65]</a></sup> Coffee is used in various dishes as a <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spice</a> or <a href="/wiki/Seasoning" title="Seasoning">seasoning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans-65">[65]</a></sup> Breakfast dishes are often reheated leftovers from the previous evening's meal, and <a href="/wiki/Omelettes" class="mw-redirect" title="Omelettes">omelettes</a> are popular.<sup id="cite_ref-Becker_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Becker-66">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Football (soccer) is the most famous sport in São Tomé and Principe, the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe_national_football_team" title="São Tomé and Príncipe national football team">São Tomé and Príncipe national football team</a> is the national <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> team of São Tomé and Príncipe and is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9an_Football_Federation" title="São Toméan Football Federation">São Toméan Football Federation</a>. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">Confederation of African Football</a> (CAF) and <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Chabal" title="Patrick Chabal">Chabal, Patrick</a> (ed.) 2002. <i>A history of postcolonial Lusophone Africa.</i> London: C. Hurst. 
        <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-85065-589-8" title="Special:BookSources/1-85065-589-8">1-85065-589-8</a> – Overview of the decolonization of Portugal's African colonies, and a chapter specifically about São Tomé and Príncipe's experience since the 1970s.</li> 
       <li>Eyzaguirre, Pablo B. "The independence of São Tomé e Príncipe and agrarian reform." <i>Journal of Modern African Studies</i> 27.4 (1989): 671–678.</li> 
       <li>Frynas, Jędrzej George, Geoffrey Wood, and Ricardo MS Soares de Oliveira. "Business and politics in São Tomé e Príncipe: from cocoa monoculture to petro‐state." <i>African Affairs</i> 102.406 (2003): 51–80. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.persee.fr/doc/luso_1257-0273_2003_num_10_1_1542">online</a></li> 
       <li>Hodges, Tony, and Malyn Dudley Dunn Newitt. <i>São Tomé and Príncipe: from plantation colony to microstate</i> (Westview Press, 1988).</li> 
       <li>Keese, Alexander. "Forced labour in the 'Gorgulho Years': Understanding reform and repression in Rural São Tomé e Príncipe, 1945–1953." <i>Itinerario</i> 38.1 (2014): 103–124.</li> 
       <li>Tomás, Gil, et al. "The peopling of Sao Tome (Gulf of Guinea): origins of slave settlers and admixture with the Portuguese." <i>Human biology</i> 74.3 (2002): 397–411.</li> 
       <li>Weszkalnys, Gisa. "Hope &amp; oil: expectations in São Tomé e Príncipe." <i>Review of African Political Economy</i> 35.117 (2008): 473–482. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.academia.edu/download/38851914/Weszkalnys_Hope_and_Oil_published.pdf">online</a></li>
